<div id="review_9368367" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9368367" />
    <a title="Paula" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/253624-paula"><img alt="Paula" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9368367?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula" href="/user/show/253624-paula">Paula</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9368367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8969685860046056509">I couldn't resist picking up this book, with a lurking shark made completely out of text on the first page. I'm a big believer of judging books by covers, and once again I am proven right. The Raw Shark Texts is like several books you've read, and yet is completely different. It plays with the concept of words like "The Phantom Tollbooth," and its underground is vaguely similar to that of Gaiman's "Neverwhere." The plot starts out as "Memento," morphs into "The Matrix" and ends with "Jaws." Conf</span>
  <span id="freeText8969685860046056509" style="display:none">I couldn't resist picking up this book, with a lurking shark made completely out of text on the first page. I'm a big believer of judging books by covers, and once again I am proven right. The Raw Shark Texts is like several books you've read, and yet is completely different. It plays with the concept of words like "The Phantom Tollbooth," and its underground is vaguely similar to that of Gaiman's "Neverwhere." The plot starts out as "Memento," morphs into "The Matrix" and ends with "Jaws." Confused? Don't worry, it all melds together pretty well (and surprisingly).<br /><br />Eric Sanderson wakes up not knowing who or where he is. Letters from the first Eric Sanderson soon arrive in the mail, attempting to describe his most peculiar situation. Eric is being pursued by a Ludovician, one of the "conceptual fish" that swim through the flow of human ideas. This shark, however, is ruthless, and will continue to hunt him until he has no memory or being left. While evading the Ludovician, he's kept busy hunting down obscure scientists through unspace and reconciling his ex-girlfriend (dead) with his guide, who just happen to share many similar traits. <br /><br />Although his style is nothing spectacular, I was continually delighted with the new and unusual ideas that kept popping up consistently from beginning to end. It's a long-ish book, but it held my attention. He has fun with typography and there's even a flipbook (which helps cut down on the pages). If the connection between words, ideas and power intrigues you, you could do worse than The Raw Shark Texts. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8969685860046056509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703606-donald?shelf=2008">2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer26402737&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26402737" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3083942238412539220">First, I'd like to say that the only thing tying this to 'House of Leaves' is that they can be termed concept novels, books that use words to further the texture of the story. Steven Hall has a great ability to tell a story and didn't need the high concept texturizing, but it was a cool deal anyway.<br/><br/>I noticed the similarity of 'Raw Shark' to 'Rorschach' right away. I'm not sure if that was intentional or not, it probably was. And like the relatively famous ink blot tests I'm not sure what happene</span>
  <span id="freeText3083942238412539220" style="display:none">First, I'd like to say that the only thing tying this to 'House of Leaves' is that they can be termed concept novels, books that use words to further the texture of the story. Steven Hall has a great ability to tell a story and didn't need the high concept texturizing, but it was a cool deal anyway.<br /><br />I noticed the similarity of 'Raw Shark' to 'Rorschach' right away. I'm not sure if that was intentional or not, it probably was. And like the relatively famous ink blot tests I'm not sure what happened. It comes down to my interpretation of things.<br /><br />The novel could be taken on a very surface level, what you read is what you get. But there is a notion, either real or imagined, that this is a novel of perception and what really happened is revealed in the postcard to Dr. Randle at the end. The rest of it might have been a sort of 'Oz'.<br /><br />The last bit of the novel reads like a script of the ending of the movie 'Jaws'. But I think it almost had to. There seems to be a leaning, in literature, to reference existing books and movies. There are other movie references in this novel: Star Trek (full speed ahead Mr. Scout (Scott)), Dr. Fidorous calls Scout - Dorothy, Eric - Tin Man, and Ian the cat - Toto from the 'Wizard of Oz', at one point there is mention of the notion that Sherlock Holmes wasn't particularly intelligent - that he had a stupid assistant. And there is a laundry list of books mentioned, many of which begin with 'Zen and the'...<br /><br />'The Raw Shark Texts' is a thriller, a journey, a love story, and a book to experience for its feel and style, and for its depth.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3083942238412539220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_348708756" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/348708756" />
    <a title="Chad Post" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/173190-chad-post"><img alt="Chad Post" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491332520p2/173190.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/348708756?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chad Post" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chad Post" href="/user/show/173190-chad-post">Chad Post</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781847671745" href="/book/show/2081374.The_Raw_Shark_Texts">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer348708756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14762293960733714015">I read this mainly because it's discussed in N. Katherine Hayles's "How We Think" (which I'm greatly enjoying). It probably doesn't deserve four stars--the ending is kind of crappy, and at times it feels a bit self-satisfied, a bit like a Charlie Kaufman movie--but it is a very "readerly" book. <br/><br/>This is a concept Kerri Pierce shared with me not too long ago. For anyone who reads tons of "difficult" or "heady" books for their job or career or whatever, you're probably already familiar with this co</span>
  <span id="freeText14762293960733714015" style="display:none">I read this mainly because it's discussed in N. Katherine Hayles's "How We Think" (which I'm greatly enjoying). It probably doesn't deserve four stars--the ending is kind of crappy, and at times it feels a bit self-satisfied, a bit like a Charlie Kaufman movie--but it is a very "readerly" book. <br /><br />This is a concept Kerri Pierce shared with me not too long ago. For anyone who reads tons of "difficult" or "heady" books for their job or career or whatever, you're probably already familiar with this concept. "Readerly" books are those books that are fun to read, that are smart without being overly cerebral, that are good, but not stylistically sophisticated, that are a sort of break from the high-minded stuff, but aren't exactly popcorn. <br /><br />So yeah, The Raw Shark Texts is one of those books for me. It's got the high concept of something like Tom McCarthy's Remainder, but the execution is less rigorous. (And the ending is fairly disappointing.) The idea of a conceptual shark relentlessly pursuing a damaged man and destroying his memories is a great set-up, but I have to say that after this idea is laid out, it doesn't really progress that much, which is kind of unfortunate, but is what it is. <br /><br />Anyway, I'd give this a 6.8-7.2 if GoodReads worked on a 10 point scale. Somewhere between 3 and 4 stars . . . And worth reading for the smart entertainment value. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14762293960733714015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_34168375" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34168375" />
    <a title="Ryan Chapman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18213-ryan-chapman"><img alt="Ryan Chapman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558356279p2/18213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34168375?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan Chapman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan Chapman" href="/user/show/18213-ryan-chapman">Ryan Chapman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18213-ryan-chapman?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34168375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13670438333976904908">I'd pair this with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/101334.Remainder' title='Remainder by Tom McCarthy' rel='nofollow noopener'> Remainder</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/30757.Tom_McCarthy' title='Tom McCarthy' rel='nofollow noopener'> Tom McCarthy</a>: debut novels from the UK by men taking on conceptual literary frameworks. Their work isn't influenced by film so much as engaged by the medium itself. It's certainly not for everyone. In fact, I hated <i>Remainder</i> for the first few months after reading. But I recognize the book--and by extension this one as well--for what is: an avant-garde novel in the 21st century. <br/><br/>This book isn't as finely balanced as it could be, and many of the romantic scenes ar</span>
  <span id="freeText13670438333976904908" style="display:none">I'd pair this with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/101334.Remainder" title="Remainder by Tom McCarthy" rel="nofollow noopener"> Remainder</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/30757.Tom_McCarthy" title="Tom McCarthy" rel="nofollow noopener"> Tom McCarthy</a>: debut novels from the UK by men taking on conceptual literary frameworks. Their work isn't influenced by film so much as engaged by the medium itself. It's certainly not for everyone. In fact, I hated <i>Remainder</i> for the first few months after reading. But I recognize the book--and by extension this one as well--for what is: an avant-garde novel in the 21st century. <br /><br />This book isn't as finely balanced as it could be, and many of the romantic scenes are so cheesy they may as well be broadcast on Lifetime. But a bold experiment persists for over 400 pages: what are all stories but failures to portray anything real? What if, then, you constructed your own elaborate story to deal with personal trauma? Only you don't know you've constructed it, or, maybe you didn't at all, or... well, this is where the genius of the book resides. Also, there's sharks. <br /><br />The idea of conceptual fish I'll leave for you to discover on your own. Let's just say the more you buy into the hokum, the more you're rewarded in the end. It's a brilliant tightrope walk of the unreliable narrator (and unreliable text) on the high end, and your basic thriller plot (with chases! and explosions! and SHARKS!) on the low end. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13670438333976904908" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iUwRKOypoxih08UCatUJyZFfj2TO/qU7UdADrA9n2DCzanj6V/dqcAb4cWOdIAMWRwBorABzK1wKrkUdwiQqqg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HtUWwupPJFhL4M5nTqNy2P0eofXwkSXfYXqyuFLWlw4k838QURHtMOzLega5VngHK0FGPT4cq7g6BPQJn5VllA==')})
  }
